I like this place.  I got there ~2pm, and I decided to do the AYCE Sushi.  I just finished work, and I was starving.  I ordered three rolls - crazy California roll, samurai roll, and tiger roll.  They were huge!  Huge not with the rice but with the filling and topping.  They were closing at 3pm but I didn‚Äôt feel rushed.  They even came around to all the tables to make sure people place their final orders.  A couple came at ~2:50, and they were not turned away.  They were told they were closing at 3pm but could stay if they place all their orders.  They stayed.<//text>

<Review>This is my third time coming to Masu and absolutely enjoy their lunch special of All You Can Eat sushi. You saw that right: ALL YOU CAN EAT SUSHI. It's $15.95 per person. For the first round, you order two items. Then, you can order one item for the following rounds. So if you go with one more person, both of you order a total of 4 items and then a total of two thereafter. You can never go wrong with this restaurant and are definitely getting your money's worth because it's $15.95.

I went to Masu on 3/12/17, where my boyfriend and I ate 8 different types of sushi rolls. The total was about $30.

Service is also attentive, which is a plus in my book. Additionally, they're very polite and accommodating to large groups.

Parking around 3rd Ave is frustrating, but there are parking garages. Parking on weekends is free.

Try this place out if you want to experience AYCE sushi. I guarantee you won't regret it.< /Review>< Name>
Reanne Matic</Name>

< review>
All you can eat sushi for lunch for $16! Great for the price but not much in terms of variety. All rolls, no nigiri or sashimi for the price. Most of the rolls are a variation of California roll, tempura roll, etc. They do have non-sushi items included: udon soup, vegetable tempura, chicken teriyaki and chicken katsu. You're able to order 2 dishes per person initially and 1 dish per person thereafter. Service is good.</review>

<time>1614631523766<//time><rate>5< /rate><Text>When I was homeless for a few nights last month, I hung out in the underground area on 7th and Hope right in front of the Dunkin Donuts since it provided shelter once the trains stopped running from like midnight to 3~4am. During the day I'd ride the subways and buses (free WiFi on the buses, by the way) since I had nowhere else to go during the pandemic. This is a great transit hub since you can take the subway to Santa Monica or North Hollywood or even Long Beach (haven't taken the Long Beach subway yet). The few days of homelessness I experienced really helped me get acquainted with how easy and convenient it is to take public transit in Los Angeles. As a native Angeleno, I'm hoping to utilize the transit system more under different circumstances since it was way more convenient than doing the whole car thing (yikes!).</Text>< pictures>

<Review>Great location, convenient, a lot to promise.
The station will serve the blue line, expo line and red line. From here you can go to Union station, and pretty much anywhere else.
It is safe, although unfortunately it is not guarded properly for issues other than security. Many people won't pay for their fare, some will pee in the elevators and at the entrance. A lot of trash near the stairs and entrance as well.

<time>1553334005857< /time><rate>4</rate>< review>
7th/Metro Center has traffic congestion above grade and this is intersection shares a network of lines throughout the city. Expo, Blue, Red, Purple and Sliver Lines (Street Level) meet here. Any casual or occasional Metro passenger could travel to either Long Beach, Santa Monica, North Hollywood, Union Station, or Koreatown from this point of reference. It's not that complicated to get a general idea of where to travel. Nonetheless, for future reference, it's helpful to know major stations, streets, and local bus routes to clarify an exact location, as you get more experience. There's a lot of passengers from different walks of life. Usually, most people are on their smartphones and helpful if you're lost, alongside with security. Generally speaking, you should be safe and not have any issues. However, with most new habits, one could easily adjust and built familiarity.</review>

< Review>
LA TRAVEL CHEAT SHEET

To get between union station and 7th street, take either red or purple lines, (they don‚Äôt matter)

Blue (A) or expo (E) line will get you to staples center (also doesn‚Äôt matter only if you go 1 stop)

Expo (E) line takes you directly to the coliseum for USC games, and will get you to Culver City/santa Monica in about an hour

Blue (A) line cuts through the roughest parts of town, gets you to Long Beach a little over an hour, connect to the green line at imperial Wilmington (105) station

The new Crenshaw (K) Line runs from Expo/Crenshaw station on the Expo (E) line if you‚Äôre looking to head south and want to avoid the Blue (A) line</Review>

Had posted this restaurant in the past but haven't gone for awhile them Covid-19 hit so now that places to eat are starting to let dine in decided to go revisit this place an was happy to still see it there since alot of restaurants had to close so seeing this place still there was nice. < review>
We came in at noon and placed order for pho, bun bo hue, and spring rolls.   We asked when we placed the order if they can expedite the order as my son fencing class resumes at 1 pm.  When it was 12:45, I approached a lady server who told me to ask someone else because she was busy!  When I came back and asked for one of the order to go because my son has to go to class, they did not look please.  Interesting because I had to go get my own napkins and utensils.   The pho was okay,  not spectacular,  although the serving size was generous.  Not being from CA, I was expecting more.  At least the bathroom was clean.  That is too bad because we were hoping to come back because we are here for the rest of the week.   The man server was pleasant.

ADDENDUM:  The bun bo hue was delicious, even at home.  I can only imagined how good it would have taste at the restaurant.  If it had not been for the service, we would have gone back.<//review>

<Review>My husband and I took a double kayak for 5 miles on the Russian River in early May. The abundant flora and fauna of the area kept the ride relaxing and entertaining. The combination of rowing and sunlight made the water the perfect temperature for cooling off. We were provided with water, hair ties, glasses savers and the staff did a great job of getting us trained on how to paddle and steer. The water level was moderately low and we hand to get out of the kayak to push ourselves over mounds of river stones a handful of times. A great activity to last ~2.5 hours or a whole day if you stop to picnic along the river.< /Review><user_name>Sasha Walker< /user_name>< resp>

< review>
Had a fabulous and relaxing time floating down the river. This trip is very laid back and peaceful, especially in the late summer when the water level on the river is getting pretty low. I did this trip in late Aug 2020 just after the big wildfires and, while a little smoky, the air was fine. I also thought the staff at River's Edge have appropriate measures in place to ensure everyone is safe from transmitting covid-19. All the equipment is sanitized after each use, everyone is wearing a mask, they have hand washing stations, and maintain a safe seating distance on the short shuttle ride. It's all good people - get outside and have some fun!<//review>

We froze the top tier for our 1 year anniversery, and after letting it thaw for a few days in the fridge (in a Tupperware style container) it came out just as moist as our wedding day. Their baked good are always a treat, and even though we now live over an hour away, we still stop by once and awhile.< /Review>

This is a very good fast casual Mexican place for breakfast lunch dinner in Mountain View.  The Mountain View special burrito is my favorite its tasty fresh juicy rich and decent price. They have good tacos and a breakfast menu. Plus good Mexican refreshment drinks like Horchata and Rose drink. You will pay few bucks more on average than Taco Bell but you will get consistently better Mexican food. In the COVID time they are operating solid take out service with quick order completion. It's been a Best of Mountain View award winner for many years! Its kind of a hidden gem in a small strip mall.<//text>

<userid>117695701051534485445<//userid><Pics>None</Pics>< text>
I'm lucky to have moved in right around the corner from the area's best burrito place! I recommend the Pollo en mole. They stew it fresh every day. One day I arrived right when they opened, and they had to ask back to the guy stirring this huge pot if it was ready yet. You may have to wait until it's properly lunch time for this treat!

La Coste√±a has been a great resource when we invite a number of friends over for a game day. We can all walk down there and everyone can have a nice custom made meal.

A lot of people get takeout here, and they keep the line moving quickly. If you want to sit (indoors, outdoors, or at their large community table), there is always plenty of room.

They are generous with their portions. They are precise with making everything as ordered.

They have vegetarian and vegan options. Ask them to customize any way you need. Since they make everything fresh they are knowledgeable about all the ingredients. It may not be a good pick, though, for those with highly sensitive allergies, as they can't guarantee there won't be cross-contamination from the assembly-line style of preparation.< /text>

< review>
This was the first e-commerce site, when Sun engineers set up a fax+ xwindows tool(xburrito) to order from your desktop in the early 1980s. It was a grocery store then where you could order your custom burrito by pointing to what you wanted. Then Run by an old husband and wife team. Now the store has moved to a new location, and the ordering process has changed. The burrito is still good, but you can no longer ask for exactly what you want. The large one can still feed a family of four. Still one of the better burrito in town<//review>

< Review>
After all these years and a location change, La Costena still boasts the best burrito in the South Bay and one of the best in the Bay Area. When it comes to burritos, the attention to detail, the quality of each ingredient, and importantly, the balance between ingredients, are second to none. La Costena offers an exquisite variety of tasty meat options and plenty of fresh ingredients. Don't be afraid to customize your burrito and order exactly what you want! My go-to is a regular carne asada burrito with refried beans, Spanish rice, "both kinds of cheeses," sour cream, guacamole, pico de gallo, and hot salsa roja. Yum! Diced jalape√±os or their "hot pico" option are fine additions if you want something spicy! Note that "regular" and "super" refer to the size of the burrito, not the ingredients.</Review>

< Text>
Don't let appearances fool you. Walk into the very sparse Mexican grocery on the corner of Middlefield and Rengstorff. In the back, you will find the source of the best burittos in the area.

La Costena is a small place dedicated to burritos. They have a large selection of proteins and other ingredients like veggies and cheeses. You choose all your ingredients as you go and watch them make it right in front of you.

They offer different sizes of burritos. Be careful when ordering the super burrito. It is actually a gigantic burrito made from two tortillas. They also offer a special every that includes a free canned drink.

They do have seating outside, which isn't bad on most evenings in Mountain View.</Text>

< Gmap_id>
0x808fb73df5dbdad3:0x977decc5fec0afad< /Gmap_id>
</record></dataset><record>
< text>
[From August 2008]

I ordered an enchilada platter today and was pretty darn pleased.

PORTION: Large, but not humongous.  That's fine :)
BEANS (whole): Cooked nicely, decent scoop, a bit watery, though (lady was too impatient to let it drain).
SALSA (mild): Don't really taste it in the mix.  To their credit, they have a selection of salsas.
GUAC: Really tasty!  Seems decently fresh.
MEAT (chicken mole):  Cooked perfectly (tender, not dry).  Nicely seasoned, but nothing amazing.
ENCHILADA:  Grilled with cheese on it, not microwaved!  This may seem like a no-duh idea, but I've been bummed at how many Mexican places just nuke their enchiladas!
CHIPS:  None offered.  Hey, that sucks :-(
COST:  Not too bad, but charging for everything extra is annoying.
DRINK:  Maybe I missed it, but no horchata and such?  WTH?
SERVICE:  Okay.  Woman wasn't particularly friendly.
PARKING:  Yeah, it generally sucks, but there were two open spaces on this Sunday afternoon.
